### Comment by [@kshalot](https://github.com/kshalot) — 2026-02-04T15:52:49Z

@ichekrygin PTAL at https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8985 (MultiKueue Synchronized Preemptions, Story 3 in your KEP). I think the simplest option for that feature is to re-use the `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt` annotation and decide what the proper API is in beta.

One relevant thing in that KEP is signaling that preemption was blocked via a condition (or some other way if the proposal is challenged). Maybe that will be useful in general and worth mentioning in this KEP? So the fact that a workload was prevented from preemption is reflected in its status. Question is whether that will also cover prevention from borrowing.

cc @mimowo @mwielgus @PBundyra

### Comment by [@olekzabl](https://github.com/olekzabl) — 2026-02-04T19:03:03Z

Just to be sure: in the MultiKueue setting, will the "cannot X" annotation prevent doing "X" on the manager _and_ on the workers?
(That's my guess, which I'd imagine to be simpler both in the mental model and in the implementation. But I'd just want to confirm my understanding).

### Comment by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) — 2026-02-04T19:56:15Z

> Just to be sure: in the MultiKueue setting, will the "cannot X" annotation prevent doing "X" on the manager _and_ on the workers? (That's my guess, which I'd imagine to be simpler both in the mental model and in the implementation. But I'd just want to confirm my understanding).

Yes, your understanding is correct, the intent is that the “cannot X” semantics apply consistently in a MultiKueue setup, both at the manager and at the worker level. That consistency is important for both the mental model and the implementation.

That said, in practice there are some nuances worth calling out.

Using `cannot-preempt` as an example: a typical MultiKueue ClusterQueue represents the aggregate (sum) capacity of the matching ClusterQueues across worker clusters. This means a workload may “fit” at the MultiKueue level, but still encounter preemption once it is placed on a specific worker cluster due to local contention or constraints.

The `cannot-borrow` case can be even more nuanced for similar reasons.

However, the general rule should still hold: if admitting a workload at the MultiKueue level would violate an admission constraint, the workload should remain pending at the manager and, by definition, should never be propagated to worker clusters.

### Comment by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) — 2026-02-04T22:38:55Z

> @ichekrygin PTAL at #8985 (MultiKueue Synchronized Preemptions, Story 3 in your KEP). I think the simplest option for that feature is to re-use the `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt` annotation and decide what the proper API is in beta.
> 
> One relevant thing in that KEP is signaling that preemption was blocked via a condition (or some other way if the proposal is challenged). Maybe that will be useful in general and worth mentioning in this KEP? So the fact that a workload was prevented from preemption is reflected in its status. Question is whether that will also cover prevention from borrowing.
> 
> cc @mimowo @mwielgus @PBundyra

Reusing `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt` for the MultiKueue synchronized-preemption story sounds reasonable to me, especially for alpha. Conceptually it aligns well with the intent of that annotation, and deferring the exact API shape to beta feels like the right trade-off.

Also, thank you for calling out another important missing detail in this KEP, namely, the need for a status condition to surface constraint violations. I’ve updated the design section accordingly. PTAL.

Without a detailed review of the “MultiKueue synchronized-preemption” issue, my initial impression is that it is well aligned with this KEP. I explicitly called out Workload API changes as a follow-up phase, and leveraging admission gates or similar mechanisms sounds totally reasonable in that context.

One immediate benefit of this KEP in the MultiKueue setting is the ability to avoid unnecessary preemption, albeit at the cost of potential starvation, without requiring any changes to the MultiKueue dispatcher(s). I demoed this exact use case during the last wg-batch meeting.

That said, I agree that a more sophisticated approach is ultimately warranted in the MultiKueue context, especially when dealing with unsatisfied constraints. In very simplified terms:

* Phase 1: attempt admission with constraints
* Wait
* Phase 2: retry admission without constraints

I am super excited about MultiKueue admission improvements and looking forward to collaborating in that area.

### Review by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) (commented) — 2026-01-28T10:56:05Z

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:122** by [@mszadkow](https://github.com/mszadkow) — 2026-01-28T10:56:05Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,219 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing or preempting other workloads, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
+I want to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or affecting how my workload may be treated after admission.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
```

  Will this require something like `labelKeysToCopy` for annotations or how would you approach the propagation of annotations from the job to the workload?

  Do I understand it correctly that this is very similar to the default settings of CQ's Preemption (reclaiming: never, borrowing: never, preemption: never) but with the per-workload granularity?

```

  These are Job-level annotations, but we also need to translate them onto the Workload object.
  While the feature is alpha it is ok to translate them as annotations on the object,  but eventually (graduation criteria) I would like to tranalate the annotation-based API at the Job level into Workload field -based API.
  
  Similarly as we have TopologyRequest in Workload based on topology annotations in Job.
  
  I imagine in Workload something like:
  
  ```
  spec:
    schedulingConstraints:
    - preemption: Never
    - borrowing: Never
  ```
  
  Another question: should the `schedulingConstraints` be at Job level, or PodSet level, because technically we could have different scheduling rules per PodSet, but maybe this is too generic.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-01-28T11:07:24Z

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:122** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-01-28T11:07:24Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,219 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing or preempting other workloads, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
+I want to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or affecting how my workload may be treated after admission.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
```

  Yeah, we should not rely on labelKeysToCopy for sure. We need to copy the annotations, but ultimatly have some field-based API on Workload object, see also: https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8844/changes#r2736125537

### Review by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) (commented) — 2026-01-28T15:10:26Z

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:65** by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) — 2026-01-28T15:10:26Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,219 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
```

  Yes, that’s a fair intuition, but with an important distinction.
  
  At a high level, admission constraints can resemble a ClusterQueue configured with preemption, borrowing, or reclaim disabled. The key difference is **scope and ownership**:
  
  * **ClusterQueue settings** are *cluster-admin policies* that apply uniformly to all workloads in the queue.
  * **Admission constraints** are *per-workload hints* that restrict which mechanisms may be used **only for admitting that specific workload**, without changing ClusterQueue policy or affecting other workloads.
  
  In other words, this proposal does not replicate or replace ClusterQueue configuration. Instead, it allows a workload to opt into more conservative admission semantics while still sharing the same ClusterQueue and its global policy.
  
  This distinction is especially useful when different workloads in the same queue have different risk tolerances, for example, some are willing to borrow or preempt to start sooner, while others prefer delayed admission over eviction or disruption.

### Review by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) (commented) — 2026-01-28T15:12:39Z

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:122** by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) — 2026-01-28T15:12:39Z

+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. +Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+

+

+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.

+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`

+

+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
```

  I agree, we should not rely on `labelKeysToCopy` for this.
  
  For the initial implementation, the intent is to **explicitly propagate the relevant annotations from the job to the Workload** as part of Workload construction, similar to how other workload-specific semantics are handled today. This keeps the behavior explicit and avoids overloading generic copy mechanisms.
  
  Longer term, I agree that a **field-based API on the Workload** is the right direction. This KEP intentionally starts with annotations to validate semantics and usage, but it does not preclude (and in fact anticipates) promoting these constraints to structured fields on the Workload once the shape stabilizes.
  
  I’ll make sure this propagation model and the possible evolution toward a Workload field-based API are called out clearly in the KEP.

```

  That makes sense, thanks for laying it out.
  
  For Alpha, I agree it’s reasonable to explicitly propagate the Job-level annotations onto the Workload, keeping the behavior simple and easy to iterate on. This feels very similar to how topology constraints started as Job annotations and later evolved into a structured Workload API.
  
  Longer term, I also agree that moving toward a **field-based API on the Workload** is the right direction. A shape like:
  
  ```yaml
  spec:
    schedulingConstraints:
      preemption: Never
      borrowing: Never
  ```
  
  seems like a natural fit for these admission-time semantics. I’ll make sure to call this out clearly in the KEP, both in the graduation criteria and future work sections.
  
  > Another question: should the schedulingConstraints be at Job level, or PodSet level, because technically we could have different scheduling rules per PodSet, but maybe this is too generic.
  
  My thinking is to keep these constraints **Workload-scoped**. Since they govern how the workload is admitted as a whole, this feels like the right level to start with. Per-PodSet constraints are an interesting idea, but they also add quite a bit of complexity, so I’d suggest keeping that out of scope for this KEP and revisiting it later if we see concrete use cases.

+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
```

  I have also been looking into #8303 + this is partially related to #8861, the "Multiple Preemptions" section, although the case of Concurrent Admission can be treated as orthogonal (cc @PBundyra).
  
  I was considering a `preemptionGates` API that would behave similarly to `schedulingGates` in Pod. This makes it more natural for the MultiKueue use-case, where a controller can "lift" the gate for a single workload. This would also allow to distinguish gates coming from several directions (i.e. a "multi-kueue" gate would be independent from a hypothetical "concurrent-admission-gate"), although it might be hard to discuss such scenarios since there's no clear use case yet.
  
  ```yaml
  # The simplest:
  status:
    preemptionGates: ["multi-kueue", "foo"]
  # or a mix of this an the proposed `schedulingConstraints`
  ```
  
  Strictly in the context of #8303, the annotations could be a starting point to build logic around them, i.e. have the MultiKueue controller manage them in the replicated worker-cluster workloads.

```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,219 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing or preempting other workloads, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
+I want to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or affecting how my workload may be treated after admission.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
```

  Thank you @kshalot for the suggestion. There is also this related KEP by @PBundyra https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8861 which is introducing "AllowedResourceFlavors". 
  
  All of them seem to serve the similar purpose  - scheduling constraint, so my gut feeling is that it would be nice to group them all by a single field

+

+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.

+

+

+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.

+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+

+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.

+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
+
+### Workload Field-Based API (Future Evolution)
+
+While the initial API is annotation-based at the Job level, the long-term intent is to represent admission constraints as **structured fields on the Workload API**.
+
+During Alpha, admission constraints are propagated from Job annotations to the corresponding Workload (initially as annotations) to allow rapid iteration and validation of semantics. As the feature matures, these constraints are expected to graduate to a field-based API on the Workload spec.
+
+A possible shape for such an API could be:
+
+```yaml
+spec:
+  schedulingConstraints:

@@ -0,0 +1,240 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing or preempting other workloads, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
+I want to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or affecting how my workload may be treated after admission.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
+
+### Workload Field-Based API (Future Evolution)
+
+While the initial API is annotation-based at the Job level, the long-term intent is to represent admission constraints as **structured fields on the Workload API**.
+
+During Alpha, admission constraints are propagated from Job annotations to the corresponding Workload (initially as annotations) to allow rapid iteration and validation of semantics. As the feature matures, these constraints are expected to graduate to a field-based API on the Workload spec.
+
+A possible shape for such an API could be:
+
+```yaml
+spec:
+  schedulingConstraints:
+    preemption: Never
+    borrowing: Never
+```
+
+The exact structure and naming are intentionally left open at this stage and will be refined based on usage feedback and consistency with existing Workload APIs (for example, `TopologyRequest`). The key requirement is that these fields capture **admission-time-only constraints** and remain unidirectional, governing how the Workload may be admitted without affecting runtime behavior or cluster-wide policy.
+
+This KEP does not propose introducing per-PodSet scheduling constraints. Admission constraints are assumed to apply at the **Workload level**, since they govern how the workload as a whole is admitted. Supporting PodSet-level constraints would significantly expand the policy surface and is considered out of scope for this proposal, but may be revisited in the future if concrete use cases emerge.
+
+### Semantics
+
+* Constraints are evaluated **only during admission**.
+* Constraints are **unidirectional**: they restrict what the workload is allowed to do during admission but do not affect how other workloads may interact with it.
+* If constraints cannot be satisfied, the workload remains pending.
+
+### Admission Flow Changes
+
+During admission, Kueue:
+
+* it evaluates admission feasibility without using disallowed mechanisms,
+* it excludes preemption and/or borrowing when computing flavor assignments and admission decisions,
+* it leaves runtime scheduling and preemption behavior unchanged.
```

  ```suggestion
  * evaluates admission feasibility without using disallowed mechanisms,
  * excludes preemption and/or borrowing when computing flavor assignments and admission decisions,
  * leaves runtime scheduling and preemption behavior unchanged.
  ```

+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
+
+### Workload Field-Based API (Future Evolution)
+
+While the initial API is annotation-based at the Job level, the long-term intent is to represent admission constraints as **structured fields on the Workload API**.
+
+During Alpha, admission constraints are propagated from Job annotations to the corresponding Workload (initially as annotations) to allow rapid iteration and validation of semantics. As the feature matures, these constraints are expected to graduate to a field-based API on the Workload spec.
+
+A possible shape for such an API could be:
+
+```yaml
+spec:
+  schedulingConstraints:
```

  yes admission fits better here

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:134** by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) — 2026-01-29T14:57:15Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,240 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing or preempting other workloads, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
+I want to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or affecting how my workload may be treated after admission.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
+
+### Workload Field-Based API (Future Evolution)
+
+While the initial API is annotation-based at the Job level, the long-term intent is to represent admission constraints as **structured fields on the Workload API**.
+
+During Alpha, admission constraints are propagated from Job annotations to the corresponding Workload (initially as annotations) to allow rapid iteration and validation of semantics. As the feature matures, these constraints are expected to graduate to a field-based API on the Workload spec.
+
+A possible shape for such an API could be:
+
+```yaml
+spec:
+  schedulingConstraints:
```

  Updated.

### Review by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) (commented) — 2026-01-29T19:03:19Z

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:313** by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) — 2026-01-29T19:03:19Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,260 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing or preempting other workloads, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
+I want to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or affecting how my workload may be treated after admission.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
+
+### Workload Field-Based API (Future Evolution)
+
+While the initial API is annotation-based at the Job level, the long-term intent is to represent admission constraints as **structured fields on the Workload API**.
+
+During Alpha, admission constraints are propagated from Job annotations to the corresponding Workload (initially as annotations) to allow rapid iteration and validation of semantics. As the feature matures, these constraints are expected to graduate to a field-based API on the Workload spec.
+
+A possible shape for such an API could be:
+
+```yaml
+spec:
+  admissionConstraints:
+    preemption: Never
+    borrowing: Never
+```
+
+The exact structure and naming are intentionally left open at this stage and will be refined based on usage feedback and consistency with existing Workload APIs (for example, `TopologyRequest`). The key requirement is that these fields capture **admission-time-only constraints** and remain unidirectional, governing how the Workload may be admitted without affecting runtime behavior or cluster-wide policy.
+
+This KEP does not propose introducing per-PodSet scheduling constraints. Admission constraints are assumed to apply at the **Workload level**, since they govern how the workload as a whole is admitted. Supporting PodSet-level constraints would significantly expand the policy surface and is considered out of scope for this proposal, but may be revisited in the future if concrete use cases emerge.
+
+### Semantics
+
+* Constraints are evaluated **only during admission**.
+* Constraints are **unidirectional**: they restrict what the workload is allowed to do during admission but do not affect how other workloads may interact with it.
+* If constraints cannot be satisfied, the workload remains pending.
+
+### Admission Flow Changes
+
+During admission, Kueue:
+
+* evaluates admission feasibility without using disallowed mechanisms,
+* excludes preemption and/or borrowing when computing flavor assignments and admission decisions,
+* leaves runtime scheduling and preemption behavior unchanged.
+
+### Interaction with Existing Features
+
+* **Preemption**: unchanged after admission.
+* **Borrowing**: unchanged after admission.
+* **Fair Sharing**: unaffected.
+* **Workload Slices / Elasticity**: constraints apply per admitted workload or slice during admission only
+  * Admission constraints apply only to the scale-up decision itself.
+  * If the additional capacity required for the scale-up cannot be satisfied under these constraints, the scale-up request remains pending until sufficient resources become available.
+
+### Test Plan
+
+#### Unit Tests
+
+* Validate parsing and defaulting of admission constraint annotations.
+* Verify admission feasibility logic for all combinations of constraints:
+
+  * allow preemption / disallow preemption
+  * allow borrowing / disallow borrowing
+* Ensure admission constraints are enforced only during admission and do not affect post-admission behavior.
+* Cover interactions with fair sharing and workload slicing where applicable.
+
+#### Integration Tests
+
+* Verify that workloads with `cannot-preempt=true` are not admitted when admission would require preempting other workloads.
+* Verify that workloads with `cannot-borrow=true` are not admitted when admission would require borrowing quota.
+* Verify that workloads without admission constraints preserve existing behavior.
+* Confirm that constrained workloads remain pending rather than being partially admitted.
+* Ensure runtime preemption behavior is unchanged after admission.
+
+### Graduation Criteria
+
+#### Alpha
+
+* Feature gated and disabled by default.
+* Admission-time constraints for preemption and borrowing are enforced only when explicitly requested by workload annotations.
+* Unit and integration tests cover all combinations of admission constraints.
+* Events and/or metrics indicate when a workload is not admitted due to admission constraints.
+
+#### Beta
+
+* Semantics are considered stable and no longer subject to breaking changes.
+* Documentation clearly describes:
+  * the admission-time-only scope of the constraints,
+  * the difference between admission constraints and runtime preemption behavior.
+* A field-based representation on the Workload spec is defined or prototyped, informed by feedback from the annotation-based API.
+* Backward compatibility is preserved for existing Job-level annotations.
+* Observability (events and metrics) is sufficient to diagnose admission failures caused by constraints.
+* Usage feedback from real workloads confirms the feature addresses concrete scheduling needs without causing confusion.
+
+#### GA
+
+* Field-based admission constraints on the Workload API are the primary and documented interface.
+* Feature gate is enabled by default.
+* No significant user confusion or misuse was reported.
+* No need for additional admission-time constraint knobs beyond those defined.
+* Backward compatibility and scheduling fairness properties are preserved.
+
+## Implementation History
+
+* Initial proposal
+
+## Drawbacks
+
+* Adds additional admission-time policy surface.
+* Requires careful documentation to avoid confusion with runtime preemption semantics.
+
+## Alternatives
+
+### Extending WorkloadPriorityClass
+
+An alternative is to extend `WorkloadPriorityClass` with a mode that disables preemption during admission.
+
+While this approach aligns naturally with preemption semantics, it has limitations:
+
+* Priority semantics are bidirectional, affecting both outbound and inbound preemption.
+* Borrowing decisions are not priority-driven.
+* Using priority to suppress preemption during admission can unintentionally make workloads more vulnerable to being preempted later.
+
+As a result, this approach is not enough to express the full set of admission-time constraints on its own.
+
+### ClusterQueue-only Configuration
+
+Encoding all behavior at the ClusterQueue level was considered but rejected, as it requires over-partitioning queues and does not support workload-specific admission intent.
+
+### Annotations vs. Labels
+
+The current proposal supports expressing admission constraints via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+
+While labels and annotations are nearly identical constructs from an implementation standpoint, they serve distinct semantic purposes in Kubernetes. Labels are primarily intended for selection, grouping, and indexing, while annotations are designed to carry non-identifying metadata that influences behavior but is not meant to participate in object selection or lifecycle management.
+
+Admission-time constraints for preemption and borrowing fall more naturally into the latter category. These constraints do not define workload identity, grouping, or affinity. Instead, they express intent about *how* a workload may be admitted into the cluster, specifically which admission mechanisms are allowed or disallowed. Using annotations better aligns with this intent-driven, behavioral nature of the configuration and avoids overloading labels with semantics unrelated to selection or indexing.
+
+We are aware that labels and annotations have different propagation semantics from parent objects to Pods. 
+However, this difference is not considered a blocker for this proposal. 
+Admission constraints are evaluated at the Workload level and do not generally require automatic propagation to Pods. 
+
+For workloads that do require pod-level integration, job owners can explicitly define the corresponding annotations on the Pod template, as is already common practice for other pod-scoped behaviors.
+
+In summary, annotations provide a clearer semantic signal for admission constraints, avoid unintended coupling with label-based mechanisms, and remain flexible enough to support pod-level use cases when explicitly needed.
```

  @tenzen-y — please let me know if this section addresses your concern around the use of **annotations vs. labels**. I’m happy to revisit or adjust it if needed.

  Just clarifying:
  
  Is there some significant difference compared to Story 2? Both cases discuss preventing disruptions caused by preempting workloads.
  
  I'm asking because Story 1 _almost_ reads as a "don't-preempt-me" feature rather than "cannot-preempt" - since the workload that is being admitted is long-running and costly to restart. IIUC Story 1 is "I don't want my workload to be preempted so I raise its priority. But that will make this workload preempt other workloads which I want to avoid as well.". Do I get that right?

+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
```

  Yes, I can totally see how it could read that way. The intent was to differentiate two use cases: "don't borrow" and "don't preempt". However, since I included "preemption" in Story 1, it effectively became a superset of Story 2. Thank you for calling this out, @kshalot!
  
  I updated the stories. PTAL, and LMK if it makes more sense now.
  Story 1 now focuses solely on avoiding borrowing for long-running workloads (where the risk is being evicted later when borrowed quota is reclaimed), while Story 2 focuses on avoiding preemption during admission (to prevent disrupting peer workloads). The two stories now cover distinct concerns rather than overlapping.

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2026-02-03T00:16:44Z

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:77** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2026-02-03T00:16:44Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,260 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
```

  Why can't peer use the very same priority for their daily jobs? 
  
  Maybe an easier to understand example would be a "gentle giant" - a job that got high priority because it should not be preempted by anyone, not because it is super urgent. It allows other to finish their stuff, and then it begins.

  How can you ensure that the job gets eventually scheduled in a BestEffort queue?

  How can you ensure that the workload is eventually scheduled in a BestEffort queue? It there is lots of unused capacity in the cluster, and a constant inflow of jobs, and the CQ safely runs well over nominal quota, the workload will become a party "wallflower", that just keeps waiting for the perfect moment that never arrives.

@@ -0,0 +1,260 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->

+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
```

  That’s a fair question, and in many cases peers *can* and probably *should* use the same priority for their routine workloads.
  
  The key reason to allow a distinction here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should *not* be disrupted once admitted.”
  
  The **“Gentle Giant”** is actually a perfect analogy for this. It describes a workload that carries a high priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted. The job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally, and only then begin execution. Its priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience.

### Review by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) (commented) — 2026-02-03T00:32:04Z

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:78** by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) — 2026-02-03T00:32:04Z

+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
+I want to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or affecting how my workload may be treated after admission.
```

  That’s a good question. The short answer is that we *cannot* strictly guarantee eventual scheduling in a BestEffort queue.
  
  This is an explicit trade-off. By opting a workload into an admission constraint, the user is deliberately choosing to limit the scheduler’s actions, for example, disallowing preemption or borrowing. In doing so, they also accept the risk that the workload may wait indefinitely if suitable capacity never becomes available.
  
  In other words, BestEffort plus admission constraints is a conscious risk acceptance: the system will make a best attempt to place the workload under those rules, but it does not provide starvation-freedom guarantees. If eventual execution must be guaranteed, the workload needs to opt into stronger mechanisms, such as allowing preemption or borrowing, or using a different queue configuration.
  
  The important point is that this behavior is intentional and transparent, not accidental, and the user is making an informed choice about where they want to sit on the fairness vs. disruption spectrum.
