+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
```

  This is essentially the same question as above, just framed with a more concrete scenario, and the answer is the same.
  
  We cannot strictly ensure eventual scheduling in a BestEffort queue under those conditions. If a workload opts into admission constraints that prohibit preemption or borrowing, it is explicitly choosing to wait for a “clean” admission opportunity. In a system with constant inflow and aggressive over-nominal utilization, that opportunity may indeed never materialize, and the workload can remain a “wallflower.”
  
  That outcome is not a scheduler failure, but an accepted trade-off. BestEffort combined with admission constraints does not provide starvation-freedom guarantees. Instead, it gives users control over *how* their workload may be admitted, at the cost of *when* it will be admitted.
  
  If a workload requires eventual execution guarantees, it must opt into stronger mechanisms, such as allowing preemption or borrowing, or use a different queue configuration. The key point is that this behavior is intentional and transparent: the user is knowingly choosing a more conservative admission model and accepting the associated risk.

### Review by [@ichekrygin](https://github.com/ichekrygin) (commented) — 2026-02-03T00:44:16Z

+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if allowed by policy. 
```

  I updated the story #@ (below), capturing this analogy. PTAL @mwielgus

+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
```

  One wallflower is not a problem, however if there is many of them they will start causing issues and confusion.
  
  What if we added a compulsory timeout to the wallflowers? Like, sure dear workload, you can wait for 1h, but after that it is enough and you should start to be more bold.

+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
```

  This is a great call-out, and I agree it’s an important concern. A single “wallflower” is manageable, but at scale, many of them could indeed lead to confusion or unhealthy queue dynamics.
  
  What you’re describing is actually quite reminiscent of what I was trying to convey during my intro and demo at the last wg-batch meeting in the MultiKueue context. There, the idea was that a dispatcher leveraging admission constraints would likely need to be *time-driven*, effectively cycling through different admission strategies over time rather than sticking to a single rigid mode indefinitely.
  
  Your suggestion feels like a natural extension of that idea. Instead of treating constraints as a strict binary (“can” vs. “cannot”), they could have a notion of **expiration**. For example, “cannot preempt for 1 hour”, or “cannot borrow for 1 day”, after which the workload becomes more permissive in order to make progress.
  
  If I understand correctly, the proposal is not to remove constraints, but to make them *time-bounded*, so workloads can start conservatively and gradually relax their admission requirements if they remain unscheduled. If that’s the intent, I think this is a very valuable direction to explore further.
  
  Do you see this as a day-1 requirement, or more as something we could evolve workload admission constraints into over time?

+## Motivation

+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals

+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+

And safe means that this workload would not be the primary target for reclamation, because it has some sort of advantage over others like earlier creation time, recently granted "I waited long enough" badge or so. The queue may still be borrowing as hell.

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:90** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2026-02-03T01:12:06Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,265 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
```

  I agree that this will help but we need proper preemption control in MultiKueue anyway - @kshalot is workin on it.

+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
```

  Looking forwarI agree that improving preemption behavior in MultiKueue is important, and it’s good to know that work in that area is ongoing.
  
  This KEP is intentionally scoped to something more narrow: allowing workloads to express *admission-time intent*, specifically whether they are willing to rely on preemption or borrowing in order to be admitted. It does not try to define or replace MultiKueue’s preemption mechanisms, nor does it assume any particular implementation there.
  
  Even with better preemption handling in MultiKueue, there are still cases where users want to say “only admit me if I fit without causing disruption, at least initially.” Admission constraints are meant to make that intent explicit, rather than implicit or inferred from priority.
  
  So I see this KEP as complementary and orthogonal. It should stand on its own, and not block on, or be blocked by, ongoing work on MultiKueue preemption control.

+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
```

  That’s an interesting idea and it’s clearly addressing a related concern. My hesitation is mainly about scope.
  
  What you’re describing shifts the focus from admission-time intent to post-admission protection and reclaim targeting, which introduces relative “safety” semantics between workloads. For this KEP, I’m intentionally keeping the goal narrower: letting workloads explicitly state whether they are willing to rely on preemption or borrowing *at admission time*, without introducing new reclaim-ordering or protection mechanisms.
  
  I think the idea could be valuable, but it feels like a separate policy discussion rather than something to fold into admission constraints themselves.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2026-02-03T20:06:19Z

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:115** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-02-03T20:06:19Z

@@ -0,0 +1,279 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing

+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+- [Goals](#goals)
+- [Non-Goals](#non-goals)

+    - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Feature Gate](#feature-gate)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Workload Field-Based API (Future Evolution)](#workload-field-based-api-future-evolution)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration Tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+    - [Alpha](#alpha)
+    - [Beta](#beta)
+    - [GA](#ga)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Extending WorkloadPriorityClass](#extending-workloadpriorityclass)
+  - [ClusterQueue-only Configuration](#clusterqueue-only-configuration)
+  - [Annotations vs. Labels](#annotations-vs-labels)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
```

  Are these annotations going to be mutable? If you don't have such a use-case I would recommend making them immutable. It seems easy to support mutability, but in the context of MultiKueue. At least for alpha, and we could re-consider for Beta or GA if business use cases arise. If you already have such a use case I would like to explicitly call it out in the "Stories" section.

- **keps/8729-workload-admission-constraints/README.md:130** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2026-02-03T20:08:00Z

@@ -0,0 +1,279 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+- [Goals](#goals)
+- [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)

+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Feature Gate](#feature-gate)
+  - [API](#api)
+  - [Workload Field-Based API (Future Evolution)](#workload-field-based-api-future-evolution)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration Tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+    - [Alpha](#alpha)
+    - [Beta](#beta)
+    - [GA](#ga)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Extending WorkloadPriorityClass](#extending-workloadpriorityclass)
+  - [ClusterQueue-only Configuration](#clusterqueue-only-configuration)
+  - [Annotations vs. Labels](#annotations-vs-labels)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/admission-constraint-preempt`, with possible values:
+  * `Always` (default): admission follows default preemption behavior.
+  * `Never`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+  * `1h`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads for at least the specified duration.
```

  I would prefer to drop it for now - we cannot express this in the API at the Job level anyway, same with the 24h below.

  💯 in agreement.

  I would expect these annotations to be **immutable**. Once the Job is created, prior to admission, the annotation must not be changed or removed.
  
  I’ll call this out explicitly in the KEP and scope it as immutable at least for Alpha. We can reconsider mutability for Beta or GA if concrete business use cases emerge and justify the added complexity.

+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing

+<!-- toc -->

+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
```

  Nit: please add a blank line; otherwise it mis-renders.
  
  ```suggestion
  * `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
  
  When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
  ```

@@ -0,0 +1,276 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->

+  - [Extending WorkloadPriorityClass](#extending-workloadpriorityclass)
+  - [ClusterQueue-only Configuration](#clusterqueue-only-configuration)
+  - [Annotations vs. Labels](#annotations-vs-labels)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* Annotations are defined at the Job level and propagated to the corresponding Workload.
+* Annotations are immutable after admission.
```

  Per [this comment thread](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8844#discussion_r2761020130), are you going to remove "after admission"?

+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* Annotations are defined at the Job level and propagated to the corresponding Workload.
+* Annotations are immutable after admission.
+
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
```

  What's the difference between "absent" and "unset" (given [immutability](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8844#discussion_r2761020130))?

+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.

+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* Annotations are defined at the Job level and propagated to the corresponding Workload.
+* Annotations are immutable after admission.

+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.
```

  I believe this states that the "default" behavior is preserved when annotation is missing or not explicitly "=true". It is orthogonally related to immutability. 
  
  The immutability requirement states that once the Job's corresponding workload has been admitted, the Job annotation should become immutable.

+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing

+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
+
+Today MultiKueue dispatching is race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either. In some cases, workloads may even be preempted on clusters that ultimately do not run them.
+
+By expressing scheduling preferences as admission constraints, a dispatcher can prefer higher-quality placements first (for example, no borrowing, no preemption), reducing unnecessary preemption and making placement decisions more deterministic.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* Annotations are defined at the Job level and propagated to the corresponding Workload.
+* Annotations are immutable after admission.
```

  I believe that comment was made before the latest KEP update. I will drop the line there.

+
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`
+* `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`
+When set to `"true"`, these annotations restrict the mechanisms Kueue may use during admission:
+
+* Annotations are defined at the Job level and propagated to the corresponding Workload.
+* Annotations are immutable after admission.
+
+
+* `cannot-preempt=true`: admission must not rely on preempting other workloads.
+* `cannot-borrow=true`: admission must not rely on borrowing quota.
+
+If these annotations are absent or unset, the default behavior is preserved, and Kueue may use both preemption and borrowing during admission as it does today.

  Ah, so by "unset" you mean values like empty string, `false` etc.?
  Then it makes sense, though I'm surprised by calling this "unset".
  
  (For me "unset" sounds like "without any value" = "absent". Or maybe "being changed from present to absent"; that's why I considered mutability)
  
  Could it be clearer like this: "these annotations are absent or have value distinct from `true`"?

+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+  
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
```

  How about mentioning @kshalot 's KEP-8303 here?
  (possibly in some "future tense", given that that KEP is currently in review).
  
  I think it'd be useful as that KEP brings new options specifically for the User Story described here
  ("avoiding (...) _unnecessary_ preemption")

+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+  
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
```

  Thank you. I'm almost happy :) but still let me share two thoughts:
  
  1. In the new version, I don't see a clear difference between User Story 3 and User Story 4.
  
     Generally, I'm sensing that the 2 distinguishable MultiKueue user stories here are these:
  
     * A. Prevent _any_ borrowing and/or preemption in MultiKueue, completely.
     * B. Prevent _unnecessary_ borrowing and/or preemption in MultiKueue; allow it in one worker if necessary for admission.
  
     And now, I'm feeling User Story 4 is entirely about B, while User Story 3 is somehow both about A and B, which makes me confused.
  
  2. In my eyes, the narration of these stories A & B in this KEP is effectively this:
  
     * For Story A: This KEP is the solution.
     * For Story B: This KEP helps in that the user can manually _reduce_ to Story A. \
       (Note though: if the user _only_ needs to avoid unnecessary _preemptions_, KEP-8303 offers a _more direct_ solution for this).
  
     By "reducing to Story A" I mean that, with this KEP, the user has to first forbid _any_ preemptions, wait to see if admission succeeded, and if not, try again having lifted the "ban". This works but isn't very convenient. 
     OTOH KEP-8303 (assuming it will stay as it is) will offer a more _direct_ solution to this, with no need of waiting, re-submitting workloads etc.

  I see the A vs B framing you’re proposing. Let me try to explain how I’ve been thinking about the distinction between Stories 3 and 4.
  
  I think the key distinction I am trying to draw with Stories 3 and 4 is that, although both operate in a MultiKueue context, they target different audiences and different layers of the system.
  
  **Story 3** focuses on the workload owner. It is about giving the workload owner the ability to prevent preemption and/or borrowing at any level. Importantly, preemption and borrowing are not exclusive to the worker-cluster level. They may also occur at the MultiKueue level during admission, before a workload is dispatched to worker clusters. KEP-8303, as currently written, focuses specifically on coordinating preemption once it occurs at the worker-cluster level. It does not address preemption that may happen at the MultiKueue level prior to dispatch; also, borrowing remains outside of its scope
  
  **Story 4**, on the other hand, focuses on the developer or dispatcher side. It explores how admission constraints could be leveraged to implement different dispatching strategies that are not currently supported in Kueue. While this KEP predates KEP-8303, the more important distinction is semantic and functional: admission constraints and preemption gates serve different purposes (as it appears). Admission constraints define feasibility and intent. Preemption gates coordinate the execution of preemption. That distinction is precisely why we have been discussing keeping `cannot-preempt` and `preemption-gated` as separate API entities.
  
  I agree that there is overlap between this story and KEP-8303, and as KEP-8303 evolves we may gain further clarity on how these pieces fit together. For now, I am keeping Story 4 intentionally open-ended as a foundation for more flexible dispatching patterns, which may ultimately incorporate or align with the outcome of KEP-8303.

+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+  
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+**Improve multi-cluster workload placement**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want to improve multi-cluster workload placement by avoiding race-based admission that can lead to unnecessary preemption across clusters.
```

  Thank you for the explanation!
  
  I missed the fact that Story 4 says "as a MultiKueue developer"; that indeed sets the distinction.
  
  LGTM.

+## Goals

+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing

+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.

@@ -0,0 +1,312 @@
+# KEP-8729: Workload Admission-Time Constraints for Preemption and Borrowing
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+- [Goals](#goals)
+- [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories](#user-stories)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Story 3](#story-3)
+  - [Story 4](#story-4)

+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Feature Gate](#feature-gate)

+  - [Workload Field-Based API (Future Evolution)](#workload-field-based-api-future-evolution)
+  - [Semantics](#semantics)
+  - [Admission Flow Changes](#admission-flow-changes)
+  - [Interaction with Existing Features](#interaction-with-existing-features)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration Tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+    - [Alpha](#alpha)
+    - [Beta](#beta)
+    - [GA](#ga)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+  - [Extending WorkloadPriorityClass](#extending-workloadpriorityclass)
+  - [ClusterQueue-only Configuration](#clusterqueue-only-configuration)
+  - [Annotations vs. Labels](#annotations-vs-labels)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+  
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+### Story 3
+
+**Enable workload owners to express multi-cluster admission intent**
+
+As a workload owner using MultiKueue, I want to express admission constraints that apply consistently at both the 
+MultiKueue manager level and the worker-cluster level, so that my workload avoids unnecessary disruption such as 
+borrowing or preemption when alternative placements exist.
+
+Today, MultiKueue dispatching is largely race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster 
+to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using 
+borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either.
+
+By expressing scheduling intent as admission constraints that are honored uniformly across MultiKueue and worker 
+clusters, a workload owner can ensure that higher-quality placements, for example, avoiding borrowing or preemption, are attempted first. 
+This reduces unnecessary disruption and makes placement behavior more predictable, without requiring global placement optimization.
+
+### Story 4
+
+**Structure multi-cluster admission attempts to reduce race effects**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want the dispatcher to structure admission attempts in phases so that constraint-respecting 
+placements are evaluated before relaxing constraints, reducing race-driven disruption across clusters.
+
+There is an ongoing parallel effort in [KEP-8303: MultiKueue Synchronized Preemptions](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8985) 
+that has significant overlap with this story. 
+While this story can be viewed as complementary, it is possible that both efforts will converge, 
+and that the functionality described here may ultimately be merged into or absorbed by KEP-8303
```

  ```suggestion
  and that the functionality described here may ultimately be merged into or absorbed by KEP-8303.
  ```

+  - [Annotations vs. Labels](#annotations-vs-labels)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+
+This KEP proposes introducing **admission-time constraints** that allow workloads to restrict whether **preemption** and/or **quota borrowing** may be used during admission in Kueue.
+
+These constraints apply **only during admission** and do not affect runtime preemption behavior, cluster-wide policy, or fairness semantics.
+
+## Motivation
+
+Kueue admission may rely on preemption and borrowing to admit workloads that exceed the nominal quota. While this behavior is desirable by default, some workloads have stricter requirements, for example:
+
+* they must not preempt other workloads during admission, or
+* they must not borrow quota during admission.
+
+Today users cannot express these constraints without overloading unrelated mechanisms such as priority or queue configuration. Doing so leads to imprecise semantics and unintended side effects, particularly because priority-based mechanisms are inherently bidirectional.
+
+This proposal enables workloads to express *how they may be admitted* without changing *how they are treated after admission*.
+
+## Goals
+
+* Allow workloads to express **admission-time-only** constraints on:
+
+  * preemption
+  * borrowing
+  
+* Preserve cluster-wide ownership of scheduling, fairness, and quota policy.
+* Avoid changes to runtime preemption semantics.
+* Maintain backward compatibility and default behavior.
+
+## Non-Goals
+
+* Allowing workloads to opt out of being preempted after admission.
+* Allowing workloads to override ClusterQueue fairness or quota policy.
+* Introducing general per-workload scheduling policies beyond admission.
+
+## Proposal
+
+### User Stories
+
+#### Story 1
+**Conservative admission for long-running or expensive workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user running long-lived or expensive workloads, I want to be conservative about how my workload is admitted.
+
+For these workloads, the cost of eviction or restart is high. I am willing to wait longer for admission if that avoids borrowing quota, reducing the risk of disruption once the workload is running.
+
+#### Story 2
+
+**Avoid admission-time preemption of peer workloads**
+
+As a Kueue user, I want my workload to be admitted only if it can fit without preempting other workloads during admission.
+
+In some environments, preempting peer workloads to admit my own job is undesirable, even if policy allows such preemption. The motivation here is not urgency, but **preemption behavior**. I want to be able to express this constraint explicitly, without changing priority or altering how my workload may be treated *after* it has been admitted.
+
+Priority is often interpreted as “who should run first,” but in practice it is equally, and sometimes more, about “who should not be disrupted once admitted.”
+As @mwielgus nicely put it, the **“Gentle Giant”** is a helpful analogy. It describes a workload that carries a higher priority not because it must run immediately, but because once it starts, it should be allowed to proceed without being preempted.
+
+Such a job is patient rather than aggressive: it is willing to wait for capacity to become available naturally and only then begin execution. In this model, priority expresses *stability guarantees*, not impatience or urgency.
+
+#### Story 3
+
+**Enable workload owners to express multi-cluster admission intent**
+
+As a workload owner using MultiKueue, I want to express admission constraints that apply consistently at both the 
+MultiKueue manager level and the worker-cluster level, so that my workload avoids unnecessary disruption such as 
+borrowing or preemption when alternative placements exist.
+
+Today, MultiKueue dispatching is largely race-driven: workloads are sent to multiple clusters, and the first cluster 
+to admit the workload wins, regardless of placement quality. This can result in workloads being admitted using 
+borrowing or preemption on one cluster, even when another cluster could admit the same workload without either.
+
+By expressing scheduling intent as admission constraints that are honored uniformly across MultiKueue and worker 
+clusters, a workload owner can ensure that higher-quality placements, for example, avoiding borrowing or preemption, are attempted first. 
+This reduces unnecessary disruption and makes placement behavior more predictable, without requiring global placement optimization.
+
+#### Story 4
+
+**Structure multi-cluster admission attempts to reduce race effects**
+
+As a MultiKueue developer, I want the dispatcher to structure admission attempts in phases so that constraint-respecting 
+placements are evaluated before relaxing constraints, reducing race-driven disruption across clusters.
+
+There is an ongoing parallel effort in [KEP-8303: MultiKueue Synchronized Preemptions](https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/8985) 
+that has significant overlap with this story. 
+While this story can be viewed as complementary, it is possible that both efforts will converge, 
+and that the functionality described here may ultimately be merged into or absorbed by KEP-8303.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+
+* **Policy fragmentation**: mitigated by limiting scope strictly to admission time.
+* **User confusion**: mitigated through explicit naming and documentation emphasizing non-runtime semantics.
+
+## Design Details
+
+### Feature Gate
+
+Admission-time constraints are introduced behind a feature gate, tentatively named `WorkloadAdmissionConstraints`.
+
+* When the feature gate is **disabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations (`kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-preempt`, `kueue.x-k8s.io/cannot-borrow`) are ignored.
+  * Kueue preserves existing admission behavior, allowing both preemption and borrowing as today.
+
+* When the feature gate is **enabled**:
+
+  * Admission constraint annotations are evaluated and enforced during admission.
+  * Disallowed mechanisms (preemption and/or borrowing) are excluded from admission feasibility evaluation.
+
+### API
+
+Introduce workload-level admission constraints expressed via annotations:
```

  So the annotations are copied 1:1 from the corresponding Job / "true Workload" created by the user, right? Maybe we could mention that explicitly
